# MapSimulator Client Parity Backlog

## Purpose

This document is the single source of truth for MapSimulator parity work against the MapleStory client.

It does three things that the old notes did not do well:

1. Separates shipped work from missing work.
2. Distinguishes broad simulator features from player/avatar parity.
3. Anchors claims to actual code seams and, where relevant, client-side reverse engineering.

## Evidence Used

### Code seams reviewed

- `HaCreator/MapSimulator/MapSimulator.cs`
- `HaCreator/MapSimulator/Physics/CVecCtrl.cs`
- `HaCreator/MapSimulator/Character/CharacterLoader.cs`
- `HaCreator/MapSimulator/Character/CharacterAssembler.cs`
- `HaCreator/MapSimulator/Character/PlayerCharacter.cs`

## Client Function Index By Backlog Area

The list below maps each backlog area to concrete client seams confirmed in IDA.
These are the first functions to inspect before changing simulator behavior.

### 1. Interaction and NPC parity

- `CUserLocal::TalkToNpc` at `0x9321f0`
- `CActionMan::LoadNpcAction` at `0x420ae0`
- `CUserLocal::CheckReactor_Collision` at `0x903d20`
- `CReactorPool::OnPacket` at `0x6cf9b0`
- `CReactorPool::OnReactorEnterField` at `0x6cf490`
- `CReactorPool::OnReactorLeaveField` at `0x6ccea0`
- `CReactorPool::OnReactorMove` at `0x6cd110`
- `CReactorPool::OnReactorChangeState` at `0x6ccd60`
- `CUserLocal::TryAutoRequestFollowCharacter` at `0x904bf0`
- `CUserLocal::TryLeaveDirectionMode` at `0x9054c0`
- `CUIStatusBar::ChatLogAdd` at `0x87aec0`
- `CUser::PetAutoSpeaking` at `0x8deb10`

Notes:
`CUserLocal::TalkToNpc` is the first concrete client seam for future NPC bridge work. `CUserLocal::Update` also shows client-side quest-alert refresh calls, emotion reset / balloon lifetime upkeep, timer refresh, timed direction-mode release, and status-bar chat logging, while `CUserLocal::TryAutoRequestFollowCharacter` covers automatic escort/follow requests and `CUser::PetAutoSpeaking` covers one of the idle-feedback surfaces tied to those broader interaction loops. A follow-up IDA scan also showed that reactor ownership is split across both local collision and a packet-owned pool: `CReactorPool::OnPacket` dispatches reactor change-state (`334`), move (`335`), enter-field (`336`), and leave-field (`337`) traffic into dedicated handlers instead of leaving all reactor lifecycle behavior on `CUserLocal::CheckReactor_Collision`.

### 2. Reactor layer-build and hit-prop ownership discovered by targeted `CReactorPool` decompile

- `CReactorPool::LoadReactorLayer` at `0x6ce630`

Notes:
The latest targeted decompile exposes a distinct reactor owner that should not stay buried inside the broader packet-lifecycle row. `CReactorPool::LoadReactorLayer` lazy-resolves `CReactorTemplate`, looks up the current state branch by stringified state id, builds the visible state layer through `CAnimationDisplayer::LoadLayer`, switches between repeat and stop playback from `CReactorTemplate::STATEINFO::m_bRepeat`, preserves timed movement against `tStateEnd` for moving states, auto-selects hit reactions through `get_hittype_priority_level` plus `CReactorTemplate::GetHitProp` when no proper event index has been fixed yet, formats and plays the per-state reactor hit sound through the StringPool template at id `2121`, and then assigns the final layer depth from the closest foothold page or z-mass plus the reactor template layer mode. That makes reactor parity split the same way as the other action-loader families already called out elsewhere in the backlog set: `CReactorPool::OnPacket` owns lifecycle and timing, while `LoadReactorLayer` owns state-layer rebuild, hit-prop arbitration, sound, and final z placement.

### 3. NPC action-loader and client-action-set parity discovered by targeted `CActionMan` scan

- `CActionMan::LoadNpcAction` at `0x420ae0`

Notes:
The targeted `CActionMan` lookup exposed another NPC-side owner that was still only implied by broader talk or actor rows. `CActionMan::LoadNpcAction` caches by NPC template, action, and client action-set index; it also has a special `nClientActionIdx == -2` branch that calls `CNpcTemplate::CalcClientActionSetIdx` before choosing the action family, applies the client default frame delay of `180` when delay data is absent, and can append reversed frames when the authored data marks that path. That means NPC parity is still missing a dedicated action-loader seam for client action-set selection and frame-table construction instead of only needing more dialogue or field-placement polish.

### 4. NPC image-entry ownership discovered by targeted `CActionMan` scan

- `CActionMan::GetNpcImgEntry` at `0x41a840`

Notes:
The same `CActionMan` pass shows the client keeps another NPC-side owner below `LoadNpcAction`: template-image resolution itself. `GetNpcImgEntry` caches by NPC template id, resolves the formatted NPC resource path through the resource manager, checks the template `link` field, recursively reopens linked NPC templates, and copies any missing top-level branches from the linked image onto the cached property tree before client-action-set selection runs. That means NPC parity is not only talk flow plus action loading; it also depends on the earlier image-entry seam that decides which normalized NPC IMG entry the action-set loader sees.

### 5. Packet-authored direction and stand-alone mode parity discovered by direct `CUserLocal::OnPacket` scan

- `CUserLocal::OnSetDirectionMode` at `0x9054f0`
- `CUserLocal::OnSetStandAloneMode` at `0x905550`

Notes:
The existing backlog tracks delayed `TryLeaveDirectionMode` release, but the direct `CUserLocal::OnPacket` re-check exposed the client-owned state-entry seam that actually drives those releases. `OnSetDirectionMode` decodes an enable byte plus a delay, clears `m_bAfterLeaveDirectionMode`, enters direction mode immediately when the packet enables it or when the delay is non-positive, and otherwise arms a delayed leave by storing `m_tAfterLeaveDirectionMode = delay + get_update_time()`. `OnSetStandAloneMode` is a separate packet-owned toggle that writes the decoded byte into the `CWvsContext` stand-alone flag rather than behaving like another window-local direction-mode alias. That owner pair is not named anywhere else in the current backlog set.

### 6. Field-state and script-message parity

- `CField::OnPacket` at `0x546d50`
- `CField::OnFieldSpecificData` at `0x52a7e0`
- `CField::OnDesc` at `0x5313d0`
- `CField::OnSetQuestClear` at `0x52c870`
- `CField::OnSetQuestTime` at `0x52b790`
- `CField::OnSetObjectState` at `0x539890`
- `CScriptMan::OnPacket` at `0x6de360`

Notes:
This packet cluster is a distinct client owner that the current backlog did not call out directly. `CField::OnPacket` dispatches field-specific data, help-message dialogs, quest-timer refresh and clear, and object-state flips from one place, while `CScriptMan::OnPacket` owns script-message delivery separately from NPC click handling or reactor collision. The dedicated quest-timer UI owner is tracked separately in the progression/utility backlog so this row stays focused on the packet source and field/script runtime.

### 7. Packet-authored field messaging and feedback parity

- `CField::OnTransferFieldReqIgnored` at `0x52f3b0`
- `CField::OnTransferChannelReqIgnored` at `0x52f5f0`
- `CField::OnGroupMessage` at `0x535490`
- `CField::OnWhisper` at `0x5448a0`
- `CField::OnCoupleMessage` at `0x5357f0`
- `CField::OnSummonItemInavailable` at `0x52f7b0`
- `CField::OnFieldEffect` at `0x53b790`
- `CField::OnFieldObstacleOnOff` at `0x535a80`
- `CField::OnFieldObstacleOnOffStatus` at `0x535b00`
- `CField::OnFieldObstacleAllReset` at `0x52c830`
- `CField::OnPlayJukeBox` at `0x537940`
- `CField::OnWarnMessage` at `0x538160`
- `CField::OnDestroyClock` at `0x52a7c0`
- `CField::OnZakumTimer` at `0x530cc0`
- `CField::OnHontailTimer` at `0x530e70`
- `CField::OnChaosZakumTimer` at `0x531020`
- `CField::OnHontaleTimer` at `0x5311d0`
- `CUserLocal::OnFieldFadeOutForce` at `0x9057f0`

Notes:
This is another packet-owned surface that the current backlog set does not describe explicitly. IDA shows `CField::OnPacket` and `CUserLocal::OnPacket` owning a broad feedback layer that sits between ordinary gameplay and the existing UI rows: group, whisper, and couple message routing feed status-bar chat and whisper-candidate state; field-effect packets drive screen effects, field sounds, BGM changes, boss HP tags, reward-roulette visuals, and object-state changes; obstacle, warning, and forced-fade packets update map presentation directly; and dedicated boss-timer plus transfer-ignored handlers show that several visible notice/timer flows are owned by packets rather than generic field-rule polling.

Additional row update for this field-feedback row: status remains `Partial`. This run kept the same WZ-first owner check against the initialized v95 IMG roots: `String/*` remains the packet text source family, `Map/Obj/etc.img/clock/fontTime` still owns the shared timer glyphs, `Map/Obj/etc.img/timer/{backgrnd,backgrndhour}` still owns the timerboard backgrounds, and `Effect/BasicEff.img/MainNotice/userReward/{Default,Notify,Appear}` still exposes the reward-roulette layer families through canvas origins plus z metadata. Using the existing direct client seam evidence for `CField::OnTransferChannelReqIgnored` (`0x52f5f0`) beside `CField::OnTransferFieldReqIgnored` (`0x52f3b0`), transfer-channel rejection packets now clear the shared exclusive transfer-request lifecycle through the existing packet-feedback callback before posting the channel-failure chat notice, matching the field-transfer failure ordering already modeled in this row instead of leaving a stale transfer request in flight after opcode `161`. Focused source coverage in `UnitTest_MapSimulator/PacketFieldFeedbackParityTests.cs` now includes transfer-channel ignored reasons `1`, `4`, and `5` consuming the transfer lifecycle before chat feedback. Remaining gap stays narrowed but still `Partial`: subtype-`9` whisper chase now builds and dispatches the native-shaped opcode-`41` transfer request through the bridge/outbox before simulator fallback, but it still cannot prove the full live `SendTransferFieldRequest` server response lifecycle without an official-session trace; subtype-`72` still writes through the simulator social-list snapshot/window invalidation path rather than byte-for-byte `CUIUserList` child-control lifecycle; screen-effect and reward-roulette playback still approximate native `LoadLayer` / COM registration beyond recovered WZ layer roots, alpha, z ordering, and offsets; obstacle visuals remain tag-driven instead of native dynamic-object visuals; summon visual fallback outside recovered generic families remains approximate when first-path `Summon.img` nodes are absent; and packet-owned `CClock` ownership still approximates native `CWnd::CreateWnd` helper/style and Cake Pie/event-board subclass lifecycle beyond recovered bounds/colors/restore/teardown guards.

### 8. `CAnimationDisplayer` social/event animation ownership discovered by function scan

- `CAnimationDisplayer::RegisterUserStateAnimation` at `0x444d30`
- `CAnimationDisplayer::RegisterNewYearAnimation` at `0x4556f0`
- `CAnimationDisplayer::RegisterFireCrackerAnimation` at `0x45a6e0`
- `CAnimationDisplayer::RegisterFollowAnimation` at `0x45ac50`
- `CAnimationDisplayer::ResetLocalFadeLayer` at `0x43b6f0`

Notes:
The function scan surfaced another client-owned surface that the backlog was not naming anywhere else. These registrations show that the client keeps several visible social/event overlays under `CAnimationDisplayer` ownership rather than scattering them only across field-message handlers or one-shot item-effect helpers: follow effects, New Year card midpoint effects, firecracker bursts, avatar-adjacent user-state layers, and local fade cleanup all pass through one animation manager. A focused source pass in `HaCreator/MapSimulator` shows partial simulator coverage through `Animation/AnimationEffects.cs` for follow animations plus packet-owned fade handling, but not a single backlog row that treats this manager as its own parity seam.

### 9. Additional animation-displayer utility and projectile owners discovered by follow-up function scan

- `CAnimationDisplayer::RegisterMobSwallowAnimation` at `0x4559b0`
- `CAnimationDisplayer::RegisterMobBulletAnimation` at `0x455b10`
- `CAnimationDisplayer::Effect_Guard` at `0x4498e0`
- `CAnimationDisplayer::Effect_Miss` at `0x449a50`
- `CAnimationDisplayer::Effect_ApplyStartDelay` at `0x449bc0`
- `CAnimationDisplayer::Effect_Cool` at `0x44a700`
- `CAnimationDisplayer::Effect_Catch` at `0x44fdb0`
- `CAnimationDisplayer::Effect_Squib` at `0x455f30`
- `CAnimationDisplayer::Effect_Transformed` at `0x450ba0`
- `CAnimationDisplayer::Effect_BuffItemUse` at `0x456020`
- `CAnimationDisplayer::Effect_ItemUnrelease` at `0x456360`
- `CAnimationDisplayer::RegisterFallingAnimation` at `0x459b40`
- `CAnimationDisplayer::RegisterExplosionAnimation` at `0x45a1d0`

Notes:
The latest IDA function scan exposed another cluster of animation-displayer owners that is not covered by the existing social/follow row or the progression backlog's production/enhancement row. These functions sit on visible utility, item-use, mob-projectile, field-falling, explosion, guard/miss, catch, cooldown, and mob special-effect surfaces. The follow-up xref check keeps them grouped for now instead of creating duplicate combat or avatar sections: `Effect_Guard` is reached from `CUser::MakeIncDecHPEffect`; `Effect_Miss` is reached from `CField_SnowBall::Update`, `CMob::ShowDamage`, `CSummoned::MakeIncDecHPEffect`, and `CUser::MakeIncDecHPEffect`; `Effect_ApplyStartDelay` is reached from `CMob::DoAttack` and `CMob::OnSpecialEffectBySkill`; `Effect_Cool` is reached from `CWvsContext::OnSessionValue`; `Effect_Catch` is reached from `CMob::ShowCatchEffect`; and `Effect_Squib` / `Effect_Transformed` are helper-style owners reached from `Effect_Reserved` / squib update paths rather than direct backlog seams yet. Nearby duplicates are intentionally left with their existing owners: `Effect_FullChargedAngerGauge` stays in backlog 6, `Effect_CashItemGachapon` stays in backlog 8, and `Effect_RewardRullet` stays under the packet-owned field-feedback row in this document. The remaining functions should stay grouped as a shared animation-manager backlog item until WZ and caller evidence proves which ones belong under more specific field, combat, progression, or packet-owned utility rows.

### 10. Packet-authored field utility parity discovered by direct `CField::OnPacket` scan

- `CField::OnBlowWeather` at `0x5468f0`
- `CField::OnAdminResult` at `0x53bc20`
- `CField::OnQuiz` at `0x537a90`
- `CField::OnStalkResult` at `0x539910`
- `CQuickslotKeyMappedMan::OnInit` at `0x6c6130`
- `CField::OnFootHoldInfo` at `0x53a810`
- `CField::OnRequestFootHoldInfo` at `0x52ddd0`

Notes:
`HaCreator/MapSimulator` keeps this row on the dedicated `PacketFieldUtilityRuntime` plus `MapSimulator.PacketOwnedFieldUtilityParity.cs` owner seam for `CField::OnPacket` field utilities. `OnBlowWeather` (`158`) drives packet-authored weather and message overrides; `OnAdminResult` (`160`) stays on the client-owned chat/minimap path, including subtype `41` as the no-payload minimap hide branch confirmed by direct IDA (`CUIMiniMap::SetShowMiniMap(0)` then `ToggleMap()`); `OnQuiz` (`161`) resolves `Etc/OXQuiz.img` question and answer text, uses the `UI/StatusBar2.img/mainBar/notice` asset, keeps the client `CUIStatusBar::SetProblem` notice lifetime of `0x1388` (`5000`) ms, and leaves the `30` second event timer on the question-side owner only; `OnStalkResult` (`172`) updates stalk/follow markers; `CQuickslotKeyMappedMan::OnInit` (`175`) follows the client `Decode1` plus `DecodeBuffer(..., 0x20)` shape so the simulator hydrates eight DIK-style quickslot codes into both labels and live `PlayerInput` bindings; and `OnFootHoldInfo` (`176`) / `OnRequestFootHoldInfo` (`177`) keep packet decode/build helpers plus the client-shaped opcode-`270` outbound payload builder `(state, curX, curY, reverseV, reverseH)` with no count or name text in the reply body. The dynamic-foothold seam still prefers live `DynamicFootholdSystem` state over stale cached packet rows, and the packet-owned snapshot name helper keeps the WZ-authored `oS/l0/l1/l2` object contract while omitting the synthetic zero-piece segment and preserving nonzero `piece` values. Focused regression coverage is now actually on disk in `UnitTest_MapSimulator/PacketFieldUtilityParityTests.cs` for admin-result subtype `41`, quickslot init default/custom decode, foothold-info round-trip decode of the verified nonzero-piece authored name, opcode-`270` payload tuple encoding, direct-send/fallback-send/deferred-bridge dispatch shaping, and zero-piece/nonzero-piece snapshot naming. A targeted WZ re-check of the extracted tutorial-family dynamic contracts in `Map/Map0/003000000`, `003000100`, and `003000200` still does not surface authored `name`, `objName`, or singular `tag` overrides on those dynamic objects; the outbound foothold snapshot name stays on the WZ-backed `oS/l0/l1/l2[/piece]/x,y` form there, with plural `tags` remaining extra metadata only. Remaining gap: the outbound foothold-response injection is still not proven end-to-end against a captured official live session in this workspace, and the broader extracted dynamic-foothold map set outside the rechecked tutorial-family contracts still has not been exhaustively re-verified for rarer client-owned outbound name separators or authored override cases.

Additional row update for this field-utility row: status remains `Partial`. This run kept WZ evidence first against `E:\MapleStory\WzExport\v95_2`: `Etc/OXQuiz.img` category/problem ownership, the `UI/StatusBar2.img/mainBar/notice` `27x21` status notice canvas, and sampled dynamic foothold object-contract naming remain the evidence base for the existing packet utility seam. Additional row update for this field-utility row: status remains `Partial`. This pass stayed in the existing `DynamicFootholdSystem` / packet-owned field-utility seam and further narrowed diagonal state-`2` playback: promoted two-point diagonal packet platforms now detect when the stored packet reverse flags make the horizontal and vertical axes point toward different packet endpoints, then advance each axis through the same packet-owned endpoint-order/carry-over logic used by horizontal and vertical moving footholds instead of forcing that conflicting packet state back onto a single waypoint direction. The opcode-`270` snapshot path therefore keeps refreshing `reverseV` and `reverseH` independently after local playback turns each axis around. ### 11. Stage-transition and map-load presentation parity discovered by direct `CField::OnPacket` decompile

- `CStage::OnPacket` at `0x71b0b0`
- `CStage::OnSetField` at `0x71b150`
- `CStage::OnSetITC` at `0x71c000`
- `CStage::OnSetCashShop` at `0x71bfa0`
- `CMapLoadable::OnPacket` at `0x61fd80`
- `CMapLoadable::OnSetBackEffect` at `0x620160`
- `CMapLoadable::OnSetMapObjectVisible` at `0x61fe40`
- `CMapLoadable::OnClearBackEffect` at `0x620150`

Notes:
The same `CField::OnPacket` decompile also hands packet families `141` to `146` to two owners that must stay explicit across backlog boundaries. `CStage::OnPacket` owns the stage-switch family for field, ITC, and Cash Shop transitions instead of leaving those jumps implied by login or UI code, while `CMapLoadable::OnPacket` owns packet-authored map back-effects, object-visibility toggles, and back-effect clears instead of treating them as generic field-effect fallout. That is a separate packet surface above the more specific field-feedback, field-state, and cash-stage rows; backlog 11 now links this same handoff from `CLogin::OnPacket` and keeps detailed implementation ownership merged here.

### 12. Passenger passive-move parity discovered by direct `CUserLocal::OnPacket` scan

- `CUser::OnPassiveMove` at `0x8dea10`

Notes:
The same `CUserLocal::OnPacket` re-check also exposed one missing follow-adjacent owner that should not stay buried under request and failure handling alone. `CUser::OnPassiveMove` only runs while `m_dwDriverID` is set, and then forwards the decoded movement straight into the passenger-side `CMovePath::OnMovePacket` seam on the attached vector controller. That makes it the client-owned movement handoff for attached passengers after the request and accept path has already succeeded, not just another follow-request dialog branch.

### 13. Context-owned stage-period transition parity discovered by targeted `CWvsContext::OnPacket` scan

- `CWvsContext::OnStageChange` at `0x9e5360`
- `CStageSystem::SetStagePeriod` at `0x71ec40`
- `CStage::FadeOut` at `0x7192b0`
- `CMapLoadable::ReloadBack` at `0x61f0c0`
- `CStage::FadeIn` at `0x718cd0`

Notes:
The targeted `CWvsContext::OnPacket` pass exposed one more stage-transition owner that should not stay implied by the `CField::OnPacket` / `CStage::OnSetField` rows alone. `CWvsContext::OnStageChange` decodes the target stage-period string plus mode byte, forwards them into `CStageSystem::SetStagePeriod`, and when the active stage is a field it immediately runs the client fade-out, `CMapLoadable::ReloadBack`, and fade-in chain on that live stage. That is a separate context-owned presentation handoff above the packet-owned field/stage dispatcher already tracked later in this document, not just another variant of `SetField`.

### 14. Initial-quiz utility owner parity discovered by targeted `CUIInitialQuiz` lookup

- `CUIInitialQuiz::OnCreate` at `0x78e720`
- `CUIInitialQuiz::Draw` at `0x78e9a0`
- `CUIInitialQuiz::Update` at `0x79c390`
- `CWvsContext::OnInitialQuiz` at `0x9ffad0`

Notes:
The broader script-message row already tracks packet decode, runtime sync, and the current WZ-backed owner preview, but a targeted IDA lookup shows there is still a separate client owner family underneath that packet bridge. `CWvsContext::OnInitialQuiz` is the context-owned entry point that opens or closes the quiz on client mode changes, while `CUIInitialQuiz::{OnCreate,Draw,Update}` prove the quiz is a dedicated utility owner with its own layout, timer/update cadence, and draw lifecycle rather than only an NPC-overlay sidecar. That owner is still absent from the backlog index today, so the current document overstates quiz parity if it stops at `CScriptMan::OnPacket` and the simulator preview seam alone.

## Current State Summary

MapSimulator is no longer "missing player simulation".
The project already has:

- A playable local character with foothold, ladder, rope, swim, fly, jump, prone, hit, death, and respawn states.
- Character WZ loading for body, head, face, hair, equipment, weapon overlays, z-map ordering, and slot-visibility conflicts.
- A working generic skill system with job skill loading, buffs, cooldowns, projectiles, hit effects, and quick-slot assignment.
- Mob and drop pools, hidden portal support, damage number rendering from WZ assets, mob HP bars, and boss HP bars.
- Several field-effect systems and special field implementations that are already present in the current simulator.

The real parity gap is no longer "does the simulator have a feature at all?".
The gap is now "how closely does the current implementation match client behavior, data selection, timing, and fallback rules?".

## Recent Progress Summary

Recent implementation progress has been folded into the backlog tables below instead of being tracked as a separate changelog.
The main baseline updates worth keeping visible are:

- Avatar parity moved out of the stub phase: action coverage, rare-action rendering, facial expression behavior, and anchor fallback rules are implemented, while mount and transform handling is partially in place.
- Skill parity is broader than the old notes implied: the simulator now loads and casts the full player skill catalog, supports runtime job swaps, shows buff and cooldown feedback, and covers more movement-family and summon behavior.
- Physics and movement now have real runtime seams for ladder lookup, float collision, movement-path snapshots, and moving-platform foothold sync.
- Combat and UI both shifted from "missing feature" to "refinement": HP indicators, damage rendering, status-bar layout, warning flashes, chat strip behavior, skill UI layout, and tooltip reuse all exist but still need client-accurate polish.
- NPC and quest interaction now have a usable simulator baseline through dialogue overlays, quest lists, and common quest-state mutations, but full scripting and inventory-backed requirements remain incomplete.

and client evidence second from `CCurseProcess::SearchSubstring` (`0x7469e0`) plus `CCurseProcess::FilterChar` (`0x746a50`) / `CCurseProcess::ConvertString` (`0x746c50`). The simulator now binds swindle text encoding to the same Windows ANSI code page used by `IsDBCSLeadByteEx` (`GetACP`) instead of relying on `Encoding.Default`, so byte filtering, DBCS lead-byte stepping, and keyword matching stay on one ACP-owned lane that mirrors the ## Priority Order

If the goal is visible parity first, the next work should be sequenced like this:

1. Avatar parity pass:
   Validate default asset selection, client-managed overlay/effect layers, and remaining action coverage against WZ and client behavior.
2. Skill execution pass:
   Implement queued follow-up, repeat-skill, bound-jump, rocket-booster teardown, and movement-coupled shoot families rather than extending the generic cast path indefinitely.
3. UI feedback pass:
   Add quick-slot validation, quest or balloon feedback, chat surfaces, and complete skill-window behavior.
4. Movement refinement pass:
   Remove the remaining ladder/float stubs, add passive transfer-field handoff, and tighten platform/dynamic foothold sync.
5. Interaction pass:
   Add NPC talk/quest flow, follow and direction-mode handling, and richer reactor interactions.
6. Reactor loader pass:
   Split reactor state-layer rebuild and hit-prop ownership out from the existing packet-runtime row before more reactor work gets documented only as packet timing or collision polish.
7. Scripted field-state pass:
   Add the packet-owned bridge for field help messages, quest timers, quest-clear resets, and object-state flips before layering more one-off script behavior onto NPC or reactor seams.
8. Packet-feedback pass:
   Add the packet-owned field messaging, warn-dialog, forced-fade, obstacle, field-effect, and boss-timer surface before more status-bar or field-overlay polish is tracked as isolated UI work.
9. Shared animation-manager utility pass:
   Run a targeted WZ/caller pass for the newly indexed `CAnimationDisplayer` utility, item-use, mob-projectile, falling, and explosion owners before folding any of them into narrower field, combat, item, or utility rows.
10. Field-utility packet pass:
   Add the packet-owned weather/admin-result/quiz/stalk-result, quickslot-init, and foothold-info surface before those handlers get misfiled under unrelated UI or field rows.
11. Stage/map-load packet pass:
   Add the packet-owned `CStage` and `CMapLoadable` bridge for field or Cash Shop or ITC stage switches plus back-effect/object-visibility mutations before those transitions get scattered across login, field-effect, or cash-stage rows.

## Working Rule For Future Updates

Update this file directly, and always classify each item as one of:

- `Implemented`
- `Partial`
- `Missing`

That keeps the backlog honest and prevents already-shipped work from reappearing as "missing".
